<p><b>Garbiñe Muguruza Blanco</b> (<small>Spanish pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[ɡarˈβiɲe muɣuˈɾuθa]</a></span>, <small>Basque pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Basque" title="Help:IPA for Basque">[ɡarˈβiɲe muˈɣuɾuˌs̻a]</a></span>; born 8 October 1993 in <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">Caracas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>) is a <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a>-<a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuelan</a> professional tennis player who represents Spain in tennis competitions and turned professional in 2012. She has won three singles titles, most notably at the <a href="/wiki/2016_French_Open" title="2016 French Open">2016 French Open</a> where she beat world No. 1 <a href="/wiki/Serena_Williams" title="Serena Williams">Serena Williams</a> in the final. By virtue of winning her first <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> title in Paris, Muguruza became just the second player of either gender born in the 1990s to win a Grand Slam title after <a href="/wiki/Petra_Kvitov%C3%A1" title="Petra Kvitová">Petra Kvitová</a> first did so at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2011 Wimbledon Championships">2011 Wimbledon Championships</a>. She achieved her career-high world ranking of No. 2 after the French Open.</p>
<p>Equipped with powerful groundstrokes and an aggressive game style, Muguruza first came into prominence by reaching the fourth round of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Australian_Open" title="2014 Australian Open">2014 Australian Open</a>, where she scored an upset over <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Wozniacki" title="Caroline Wozniacki">Caroline Wozniacki</a> en route. She then defeated Serena Williams in the second round of the <a href="/wiki/2014_French_Open" title="2014 French Open">French Open</a> that same year, beating the world No. 1 in straight sets en route to the quarterfinals. In 2015, she won the <a href="/wiki/2015_China_Open_(tennis)" title="2015 China Open (tennis)">China Open</a> and reached her first Grand Slam final at <a href="/wiki/2015_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2015 Wimbledon Championships">Wimbledon</a>. She also qualified for her first <a href="/wiki/2015_WTA_Finals" title="2015 WTA Finals">WTA Finals</a> in 2015, scoring a perfect winning record in the round-robin stage before falling out in the semifinals to eventual champion <a href="/wiki/Agnieszka_Radwa%C5%84ska" title="Agnieszka Radwańska">Agnieszka Radwańska</a>.</p>
<p>Muguruza has been successful in doubles, winning five titles, finishing runner-up at the <a href="/wiki/2015_WTA_Finals" title="2015 WTA Finals">2015 WTA Finals</a> and reaching the <a href="/wiki/2014_French_Open" title="2014 French Open">2014 French Open</a> semifinals. She achieved those results with her compatriot, <a href="/wiki/Carla_Su%C3%A1rez_Navarro" title="Carla Suárez Navarro">Carla Suárez Navarro</a>.</p>
<p>She is currently ranked No. 7 in singles and No. 30 in doubles.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Muguruza was born in <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">Caracas</a>, Venezuela, in 1993 to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a>-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basque_people" title="Basque people">Basque</a> father, José Antonio Muguruza from <a href="/wiki/Eibar" title="Eibar">Eibar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gipuzkoa" title="Gipuzkoa">Gipuzkoa</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venezuelan_people" title="Venezuelan people">Venezuelan</a> mother, Scarlet Blanco, and has two elder brothers named Asier and Igor. She has dual Venezuelan-Spanish nationality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> She began playing tennis at the age of three and, after moving to Spain with her family in 1999 when she was six years old,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Muguruza trained at the Bruguera Tennis Academy near Barcelona. Her tennis idol is <a href="/wiki/Serena_Williams" title="Serena Williams">Serena Williams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dream_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-dream-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wtabio_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-wtabio-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012.E2.80.932013:_Start_of_career">2012–2013: Start of career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2012–2013: Start of career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Muguruza was given a wildcard at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Sony_Ericsson_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Singles" title="2012 Sony Ericsson Open – Women's Singles">2012 Miami Open</a> for her first WTA main draw appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wildcard_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-wildcard-6">[6]</a></sup> There, she upset former world No. 2 <a href="/wiki/Vera_Zvonareva" title="Vera Zvonareva">Vera Zvonareva</a> and former world No. 10 <a href="/wiki/Flavia_Pennetta" title="Flavia Pennetta">Flavia Pennetta</a> in the second and third rounds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wildcard_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-wildcard-6">[6]</a></sup> before losing to the eventual champion, <a href="/wiki/Agnieszka_Radwa%C5%84ska" title="Agnieszka Radwańska">Agnieszka Radwańska</a> in straight sets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2013_BNP_Paribas_Open" title="2013 BNP Paribas Open">2013 Indian Wells Masters</a>, Muguruza made it through two rounds of qualifying and then made her way to the fourth round of the main draw, where she fell to <a href="/wiki/Angelique_Kerber" title="Angelique Kerber">Angelique Kerber</a>. She was then awarded a main draw wildcard into the <a href="/wiki/WTA_Premier_tournaments" title="WTA Premier tournaments">Premier Mandatory</a> event in <a href="/wiki/Miami_Open_(tennis)" title="Miami Open (tennis)">Miami</a> for the second consecutive year, where she advanced to the fourth round, recording wins over <a href="/wiki/Kate%C5%99ina_Siniakov%C3%A1" title="Kateřina Siniaková">Kateřina Siniaková</a>, twenty-third seed <a href="/wiki/Anastasia_Pavlyuchenkova" title="Anastasia Pavlyuchenkova">Anastasia Pavlyuchenkova</a> and ninth seed <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Wozniacki" title="Caroline Wozniacki">Caroline Wozniacki</a> en route before losing to the No. 5 seed, <a href="/wiki/Li_Na" title="Li Na">Li Na</a>.</p>
<p>After Wimbledon in 2013, Muguruza underwent right ankle surgery and missed the rest of the season. She continued to train by hitting groundstrokes sitting down. She ended the year as the World No. 63 in singles and World No. 153 in doubles.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014:_First_WTA_singles_title_and_first_Grand_Slam_quarterfinal">2014: First WTA singles title and first Grand Slam quarterfinal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2014: First WTA singles title and first Grand Slam quarterfinal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Muguruza began the <a href="/wiki/2014_WTA_Tour" title="2014 WTA Tour">2014 season</a> with a quarterfinal appearance at the <a href="/wiki/2014_ASB_Classic" title="2014 ASB Classic">Auckland Open</a>, where she lost to former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_WTA_number_1_ranked_singles_players" title="List of WTA number 1 ranked singles players">world No. 1</a> and eventual runner-up, <a href="/wiki/Venus_Williams" title="Venus Williams">Venus Williams</a>. The following week, Muguruza qualified and eventually won her first <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Tennis_Association" title="Women's Tennis Association">WTA</a> singles title at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Hobart_International" title="2014 Hobart International">Hobart International</a> by defeating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kl%C3%A1ra_Zakopalov%C3%A1" title="Klára Zakopalová">Klára Zakopalová</a> in the final in straight sets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2014_Australian_Open" title="2014 Australian Open">Australian Open</a>, Muguruza recovered from a set down to defeat tenth seed <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Wozniacki" title="Caroline Wozniacki">Caroline Wozniacki</a> in three sets<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> to reach the fourth round for the first time where she lost in straight sets to the fifth seed, <a href="/wiki/Agnieszka_Radwa%C5%84ska" title="Agnieszka Radwańska">Agnieszka Radwańska</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> She and <a href="/wiki/Arantxa_Parra_Santonja" title="Arantxa Parra Santonja">Arantxa Parra Santonja</a> also reached the second round of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Australian_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2014 Australian Open – Women's Doubles">doubles event</a> where they lost in straight sets to the eighth seeds, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raquel_Kops-Jones" title="Raquel Kops-Jones">Raquel Kops-Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abigail_Spears" title="Abigail Spears">Abigail Spears</a>.</p>
<p>After a three-set defeat to <a href="/wiki/Kimiko_Date-Krumm" title="Kimiko Date-Krumm">Kimiko Date-Krumm</a> in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/2014_PTT_Pattaya_Open" title="2014 PTT Pattaya Open">Thailand Open</a>, Muguruza reached her second singles final of the year at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Brasil_Tennis_Cup" title="2014 Brasil Tennis Cup">2014 Brasil Tennis Cup</a>, where she lost in three sets to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kl%C3%A1ra_Zakopalov%C3%A1" title="Klára Zakopalová">Klára Zakopalová</a> despite having led by a set and 5–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Muguruza then lost in the second round of the <a href="/wiki/2014_BNP_Paribas_Open" title="2014 BNP Paribas Open">Indian Wells Masters</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_Sony_Open_Tennis" title="2014 Sony Open Tennis">Miami Open</a> after receiving opening round byes, but did reach the quarterfinals of the latter event in doubles where she and her partner, <a href="/wiki/Carla_Su%C3%A1rez_Navarro" title="Carla Suárez Navarro">Carla Suárez Navarro</a> lost in three sets to the eighth seeds, Raquel Kops-Jones and Abigail Spears.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Muguruza_MA14_(8)_(14239532067).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2763" data-file-width="1920" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Muguruza_MA14_%288%29_%2814239532067%29.jpg/175px-Muguruza_MA14_%288%29_%2814239532067%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Muguruza_MA14_%288%29_%2814239532067%29.jpg/263px-Muguruza_MA14_%288%29_%2814239532067%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Muguruza_MA14_%288%29_%2814239532067%29.jpg/350px-Muguruza_MA14_%288%29_%2814239532067%29.jpg 2x" width="175"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Muguruza_MA14_(8)_(14239532067).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Muguruza and <a href="/wiki/Carla_Su%C3%A1rez_Navarro" title="Carla Suárez Navarro">Carla Suárez Navarro</a> reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Mutua_Madrid_Open" title="2014 Mutua Madrid Open">Madrid Open</a>, won the <a href="/wiki/2014_Bank_of_the_West_Classic" title="2014 Bank of the West Classic">Stanford Classic</a> and later qualified for the year-ending <a href="/wiki/2014_WTA_Finals" title="2014 WTA Finals">WTA Finals</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Muguruza recovered from her first round defeat at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Monterrey_Open" title="2014 Monterrey Open">2014 Monterrey Open</a> by reaching the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Grand_Prix_SAR_La_Princesse_Lalla_Meryem" title="2014 Grand Prix SAR La Princesse Lalla Meryem">Marrakech Grand Prix</a> where she lost to the eventual champion, <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Teresa_Torr%C3%B3_Flor" title="María Teresa Torró Flor">María Teresa Torró Flor</a> in straight sets. However, she and <a href="/wiki/Romina_Oprandi" title="Romina Oprandi">Romina Oprandi</a> managed to win the <a href="/wiki/2014_Grand_Prix_SAR_La_Princesse_Lalla_Meryem_%E2%80%93_Doubles" title="2014 Grand Prix SAR La Princesse Lalla Meryem – Doubles">doubles event</a> by defeating <a href="/wiki/Katarzyna_Piter" title="Katarzyna Piter">Katarzyna Piter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maryna_Zanevska" title="Maryna Zanevska">Maryna Zanevska</a> in the final in three sets. At the <a href="/wiki/2014_Mutua_Madrid_Open" title="2014 Mutua Madrid Open">Madrid Open</a>, Muguruza lost in the second round to former <a href="/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">US Open</a> champion, <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Stosur" title="Samantha Stosur">Samantha Stosur</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> but reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Mutua_Madrid_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2014 Mutua Madrid Open – Women's Doubles">doubles event</a> with Carla Suárez Navarro where they lost in straight sets to the second seeded Italians, <a href="/wiki/Sara_Errani" title="Sara Errani">Sara Errani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roberta_Vinci" title="Roberta Vinci">Roberta Vinci</a>.</p>
<p>After a second round defeat to former <a href="/wiki/French_Open" title="French Open">French Open</a> champion <a href="/wiki/Francesca_Schiavone" title="Francesca Schiavone">Francesca Schiavone</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Internazionali_BNL_d%27Italia" title="2014 Internazionali BNL d'Italia">Italian Open</a>, Muguruza advanced to her first <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">major</a> quarterfinal at the <a href="/wiki/2014_French_Open" title="2014 French Open">French Open</a>, having handed the world No. 1 and defending champion <a href="/wiki/Serena_Williams" title="Serena Williams">Serena Williams</a> her worst lost in a Grand Slam tournament, losing only four games in the second round,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> before losing to the eventual champion, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Sharapova" title="Maria Sharapova">Maria Sharapova</a> in three sets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Muguruza also reached the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2014_French_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2014 French Open – Women's Doubles">doubles event</a> with Suárez Navarro, where the pair lost in three sets to the top seeds and eventual champions, <a href="/wiki/Peng_Shuai" title="Peng Shuai">Peng Shuai</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Su-Wei_Hsieh" title="Su-Wei Hsieh">Su-Wei Hsieh</a>. As a result of her strong performances at the event, Muguruza achieved career high singles and doubles rankings of world No. 27 and world No. 36 respectively.</p>
<p>Muguruza began her <a href="/wiki/Grass_court" title="Grass court">grass court</a> season at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Topshelf_Open" title="2014 Topshelf Open">Rosmalen Grass Court Championships</a> where she reached the quarterfinals before losing to American qualifier <a href="/wiki/Coco_Vandeweghe" title="Coco Vandeweghe">Coco Vandeweghe</a> in straight sets after leading 5–2 in the opening set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2014_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2014 Wimbledon Championships">Wimbledon Championships</a>, Muguruza was seeded twenty-seventh but was upset by Vandeweghe in the first round in three sets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Seeded sixteenth in the <a href="/wiki/2014_Wimbledon_Championships_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2014 Wimbledon Championships – Women's Doubles">doubles event</a> with <a href="/wiki/Carla_Su%C3%A1rez_Navarro" title="Carla Suárez Navarro">Carla Suárez Navarro</a>, Muguruza and her partner defeated <a href="/wiki/Ajla_Tomljanovi%C4%87" title="Ajla Tomljanović">Ajla Tomljanović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christina_McHale" title="Christina McHale">Christina McHale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monica_Niculescu" title="Monica Niculescu">Monica Niculescu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kl%C3%A1ra_Koukalov%C3%A1" title="Klára Koukalová">Klára Koukalová</a> to reach the third round where they lost in straight sets to <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Petkovic" title="Andrea Petkovic">Andrea Petkovic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magdal%C3%A9na_Ryb%C3%A1rikov%C3%A1" title="Magdaléna Rybáriková">Magdaléna Rybáriková</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Muguruza began the North American hard court season at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Bank_of_the_West_Classic" title="2014 Bank of the West Classic">Stanford Classic</a>. She defeated sixth seed and defending champion, <a href="/wiki/Dominika_Cibulkov%C3%A1" title="Dominika Cibulková">Dominika Cibulková</a> in three sets<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and unseeded <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakian</a> <a href="/wiki/Daniela_Hantuchov%C3%A1" title="Daniela Hantuchová">Daniela Hantuchová</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> to reach the quarterfinals where she lost in straight sets to the third seed, <a href="/wiki/Angelique_Kerber" title="Angelique Kerber">Angelique Kerber</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Seeded third in the <a href="/wiki/2014_Bank_of_the_West_Classic_%E2%80%93_Doubles" title="2014 Bank of the West Classic – Doubles">doubles</a> event with Carla Suárez Navarro, the pair defeated <a href="/wiki/Eva_Hrdinov%C3%A1" title="Eva Hrdinová">Eva Hrdinová</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andreja_Klepa%C4%8D" title="Andreja Klepač">Andreja Klepač</a>; <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Garcia" title="Caroline Garcia">Caroline Garcia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Shuai_(tennis)" title="Zhang Shuai (tennis)">Zhang Shuai</a> and the second seeds, <a href="/wiki/Anastasia_Rodionova" title="Anastasia Rodionova">Anastasia Rodionova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alla_Kudryavtseva" title="Alla Kudryavtseva">Alla Kudryavtseva</a> to reach the final where they defeated <a href="/wiki/Paula_Kania" title="Paula Kania">Paula Kania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kate%C5%99ina_Siniakov%C3%A1" title="Kateřina Siniaková">Kateřina Siniaková</a> in three sets to win the title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> At the following week's <a href="/wiki/2014_Rogers_Cup" title="2014 Rogers Cup">Canadian Open</a>, Muguruza overcame Canadian qualifier <a href="/wiki/St%C3%A9phanie_Dubois" title="Stéphanie Dubois">Stéphanie Dubois</a> in the first round before falling in three sets to fourth seed, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Sharapova" title="Maria Sharapova">Maria Sharapova</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2014_Rogers_Cup_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2014 Rogers Cup – Women's Doubles">doubles</a> event, Muguruza and Suárez Navarro progressed to the second round where they lost to the second seeds, <a href="/wiki/Hsieh_Su-wei" title="Hsieh Su-wei">Hsieh Su-wei</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peng_Shuai" title="Peng Shuai">Peng Shuai</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2014_Western_%26_Southern_Open" title="2014 Western &amp; Southern Open">Cincinnati Masters</a>, Muguruza lost in the first round to German qualifier <a href="/wiki/Annika_Beck" title="Annika Beck">Annika Beck</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> but reached the quarterfinals in <a href="/wiki/2014_Western_%26_Southern_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2014 Western &amp; Southern Open – Women's Doubles">doubles</a> where she and Suárez Navarro lost to <a href="/wiki/Kimiko_Date-Krumm" title="Kimiko Date-Krumm">Kimiko Date-Krumm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Hlav%C3%A1%C4%8Dkov%C3%A1" title="Andrea Hlaváčková">Andrea Hlaváčková</a> in straight sets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2014_Connecticut_Open" title="2014 Connecticut Open">Connecticut Open</a>, Muguruza upset seventh seed <a href="/wiki/Sara_Errani" title="Sara Errani">Sara Errani</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> before defeating Chinese qualifier <a href="/wiki/Peng_Shuai" title="Peng Shuai">Peng Shuai</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> to reach the quarterfinals where she lost in three sets to unseeded Italian, <a href="/wiki/Camila_Giorgi" title="Camila Giorgi">Camila Giorgi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> She and Suárez Navarro also lost to <a href="/wiki/Marina_Erakovic" title="Marina Erakovic">Marina Erakovic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arantxa_Parra_Santonja" title="Arantxa Parra Santonja">Arantxa Parra Santonja</a> in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Connecticut_Open_%E2%80%93_Doubles" title="2014 Connecticut Open – Doubles">doubles</a> event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Muguruza's next event was the <a href="/wiki/2014_US_Open_(tennis)" title="2014 US Open (tennis)">US Open</a>, where she competed as the twenty-fifth seed. However, she was upset by resurgent qualifier, <a href="/wiki/Mirjana_Lu%C4%8Di%C4%87-Baroni" title="Mirjana Lučić-Baroni">Mirjana Lučić-Baroni</a> in the first round in straight sets. She and Suarez Navarro also reached the third round of the <a href="/wiki/2014_US_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2014 US Open – Women's Doubles">doubles event</a>, defeating <a href="/wiki/Aliz%C3%A9_Cornet" title="Alizé Cornet">Alizé Cornet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Flipkens" title="Kirsten Flipkens">Kirsten Flipkens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marina_Erakovic" title="Marina Erakovic">Marina Erakovic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arantxa_Parra_Santonja" title="Arantxa Parra Santonja">Arantxa Parra Santonja</a> en route before losing to the unseeded <a href="/wiki/Williams_sisters" title="Williams sisters">Williams sisters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_(15338611192).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2155" data-file-width="2420" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_%2815338611192%29.jpg/220px-Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_%2815338611192%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_%2815338611192%29.jpg/330px-Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_%2815338611192%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_%2815338611192%29.jpg/440px-Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_%2815338611192%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

Garbiñe Muguruza at the <a href="/wiki/Pan_Pacific_Open" title="Pan Pacific Open">Toray Pan Pacific Open 2014</a> where she was a doubles finalist</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Muguruza began the Asian swing by competing at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Toray_Pan_Pacific_Open" title="2014 Toray Pan Pacific Open">Pan Pacific Open</a>. She defeated <a href="/wiki/Anastasia_Pavlyuchenkova" title="Anastasia Pavlyuchenkova">Anastasia Pavlyuchenkova</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> fourth seed <a href="/wiki/Jelena_Jankovi%C4%87" title="Jelena Janković">Jelena Janković</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Casey_Dellacqua" title="Casey Dellacqua">Casey Dellacqua</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> en route to the semi-finals where she fell in three sets to the second seed and eventual runner-up, <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Wozniacki" title="Caroline Wozniacki">Caroline Wozniacki</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Muguruza also reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Toray_Pan_Pacific_Open_%E2%80%93_Doubles" title="2014 Toray Pan Pacific Open – Doubles">doubles event</a> with Carla Suárez Navarro, defeating Pavlyuchenkova and <a href="/wiki/Lucie_%C5%A0af%C3%A1%C5%99ov%C3%A1" title="Lucie Šafářová">Lucie Šafářová</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jarmila_Gajdo%C5%A1ov%C3%A1" title="Jarmila Gajdošová">Jarmila Gajdošová</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arina_Rodionova" title="Arina Rodionova">Arina Rodionova</a> and the second seeds, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raquel_Kops-Jones" title="Raquel Kops-Jones">Raquel Kops-Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abigail_Spears" title="Abigail Spears">Abigail Spears</a> en route before losing to the top seeds, <a href="/wiki/Cara_Black" title="Cara Black">Cara Black</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sania_Mirza" title="Sania Mirza">Sania Mirza</a> in straight sets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Muguruza next competed at the inaugural edition of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Wuhan_Open" title="2014 Wuhan Open">Wuhan Open</a>, where she reached the third round of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Wuhan_Open_%E2%80%93_Singles" title="2014 Wuhan Open – Singles">singles</a>, defeating <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Teresa_Torr%C3%B3_Flor" title="María Teresa Torró Flor">María Teresa Torró Flor</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> and world No. 2 <a href="/wiki/Simona_Halep" title="Simona Halep">Simona Halep</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> en route and the second round of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Wuhan_Open_%E2%80%93_Doubles" title="2014 Wuhan Open – Doubles">doubles</a> with Suárez Navarro after defeating Torró Flor and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%ADlvia_Soler_Espinosa" title="Sílvia Soler Espinosa">Sílvia Soler Espinosa</a> in the first round<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> but was ultimately forced to withdraw from the event due to gastritis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> At the following week's <a href="/wiki/2014_China_Open_(tennis)" title="2014 China Open (tennis)">China Open</a>, Muguruza suffered a three set first round loss to <a href="/wiki/Ekaterina_Makarova" title="Ekaterina Makarova">Ekaterina Makarova</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> but reached the quarterfinals of the <a href="/wiki/2014_China_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2014 China Open – Women's Doubles">doubles</a> event with Suárez Navarro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Muguruza's final event of the year was the season ending <a href="/wiki/2014_Garanti_Koza_WTA_Tournament_of_Champions" title="2014 Garanti Koza WTA Tournament of Champions">WTA Tournament of Champions</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>. Despite going undefeated in the <a href="/wiki/Round-robin_tournament" title="Round-robin tournament">round robin</a> stage with wins over top seed, <a href="/wiki/Ekaterina_Makarova" title="Ekaterina Makarova">Ekaterina Makarova</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> third seed <a href="/wiki/Flavia_Pennetta" title="Flavia Pennetta">Flavia Pennetta</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> and sixth seed <a href="/wiki/Aliz%C3%A9_Cornet" title="Alizé Cornet">Alizé Cornet</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Muguruza fell to the eventual champion, <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Petkovic" title="Andrea Petkovic">Andrea Petkovic</a> in the semi-finals in straight sets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Muguruza finished the year ranked at career high rankings of world No. 21 in singles and world No. 16 in doubles.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015:_First_Grand_Slam_final_and_first_Premier_Mandatory_title">2015: First Grand Slam final and first Premier Mandatory title</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2015: First Grand Slam final and first Premier Mandatory title">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Muguruza_RG15_(24)_(19311051291).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2944" data-file-width="1968" height="262" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Muguruza_RG15_%2824%29_%2819311051291%29.jpg/175px-Muguruza_RG15_%2824%29_%2819311051291%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Muguruza_RG15_%2824%29_%2819311051291%29.jpg/263px-Muguruza_RG15_%2824%29_%2819311051291%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Muguruza_RG15_%2824%29_%2819311051291%29.jpg/350px-Muguruza_RG15_%2824%29_%2819311051291%29.jpg 2x" width="175"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Muguruza_RG15_(24)_(19311051291).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Muguruza reached her second <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">major</a> quarterfinal at the <a href="/wiki/2015_French_Open" title="2015 French Open">2015 French Open</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Muguruza's first event of the year was to be the <a href="/wiki/2015_Brisbane_International" title="2015 Brisbane International">Brisbane International</a> but she was forced to withdraw from the event due to an ankle injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The following week, Muguruza chose not to defend her title at the <a href="/wiki/2015_Hobart_International" title="2015 Hobart International">Hobart International</a> and competed at the <a href="/wiki/2015_Apia_International_Sydney" title="2015 Apia International Sydney">Sydney International</a> instead, where she reached the quarterfinals, defeating <a href="/wiki/Agnieszka_Radwa%C5%84ska" title="Agnieszka Radwańska">Agnieszka Radwańska</a> for the first time in her career en route.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2015_Australian_Open" title="2015 Australian Open">Australian Open</a>, she progressed to the fourth round for the second consecutive year with wins over <a href="/wiki/Marina_Erakovic" title="Marina Erakovic">Marina Erakovic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniela_Hantuchov%C3%A1" title="Daniela Hantuchová">Daniela Hantuchová</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timea_Bacsinszky" title="Timea Bacsinszky">Timea Bacsinszky</a> before falling to the eventual champion, <a href="/wiki/Serena_Williams" title="Serena Williams">Serena Williams</a> in three sets.</p>
<p>Muguruza won both of her singles rubbers in the <a href="/wiki/2015_Fed_Cup_World_Group_II" title="2015 Fed Cup World Group II">2015 Fed Cup World Group II</a>, defeating <a href="/wiki/Irina-Camelia_Begu" title="Irina-Camelia Begu">Irina-Camelia Begu</a> and world No. 3 <a href="/wiki/Simona_Halep" title="Simona Halep">Simona Halep</a> but Spain lost the tie 3–2 after Muguruza and her compatriot, <a href="/wiki/Anabel_Medina_Garrigues" title="Anabel Medina Garrigues">Anabel Medina Garrigues</a> lost the deciding doubles rubber. At the <a href="/wiki/2015_Dubai_Tennis_Championships" title="2015 Dubai Tennis Championships">Dubai Tennis Championships</a>, Muguruza reached her first WTA Premier 5 semi-final in singles, defeating qualifier <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jarmila_Gajdo%C5%A1ov%C3%A1" title="Jarmila Gajdošová">Jarmila Gajdošová</a>, twelfth seed <a href="/wiki/Jelena_Jankovi%C4%87" title="Jelena Janković">Jelena Janković</a>, fifth seed <a href="/wiki/Agnieszka_Radwa%C5%84ska" title="Agnieszka Radwańska">Agnieszka Radwańska</a> and thirteenth seed and doubles partner <a href="/wiki/Carla_Su%C3%A1rez_Navarro" title="Carla Suárez Navarro">Carla Suárez Navarro</a> before falling to the seventeenth seed and eventual runner-up, <a href="/wiki/Karol%C3%ADna_Pl%C3%AD%C5%A1kov%C3%A1" title="Karolína Plíšková">Karolína Plíšková</a> in three sets. She also reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/2015_Dubai_Tennis_Championships_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2015 Dubai Tennis Championships – Women's Doubles">doubles</a> with Suárez Navarro. The following week, Muguruza retired from her first round match against Suárez Navarro at the <a href="/wiki/2015_Qatar_Total_Open" title="2015 Qatar Total Open">Qatar Open</a> while trailing 6–5 in the first set.</p>
<p>In March, Muguruza lost to Ka. Plíšková in the third round of the <a href="/wiki/2015_BNP_Paribas_Open" title="2015 BNP Paribas Open">Indian Wells Masters</a> after a second round win over American wildcard <a href="/wiki/Irina_Falconi" title="Irina Falconi">Irina Falconi</a>. Despite this, she rose to a career high singles ranking of world No. 19 after the event. A fortnight later, Muguruza reached the third round of the <a href="/wiki/2015_Miami_Open" title="2015 Miami Open">Miami Open</a> after defeating qualifier <a href="/wiki/Sesil_Karatantcheva" title="Sesil Karatantcheva">Sesil Karatantcheva</a> but lost to the eleventh seed <a href="/wiki/Sara_Errani" title="Sara Errani">Sara Errani</a> after winning the first set.</p>
<p>Muguruza reached the second round of the three clay court events that she competed in leading into the <a href="/wiki/2015_French_Open" title="2015 French Open">French Open</a>. She lost to second seed Simona Halep in <a href="/wiki/2015_Porsche_Tennis_Grand_Prix" title="2015 Porsche Tennis Grand Prix">Stuttgart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kristina_Mladenovic" title="Kristina Mladenovic">Kristina Mladenovic</a> in <a href="/wiki/2015_Grand_Prix_SAR_La_Princesse_Lalla_Meryem" title="2015 Grand Prix SAR La Princesse Lalla Meryem">Marrakech</a> and the eventual finalist <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Kuznetsova" title="Svetlana Kuznetsova">Svetlana Kuznetsova</a> in <a href="/wiki/2015_Mutua_Madrid_Open" title="2015 Mutua Madrid Open">Madrid</a>. Muguruza and Suárez Navarro also reached the <a href="/wiki/2015_Mutua_Madrid_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Doubles" title="2015 Mutua Madrid Open – Women's Doubles">doubles</a> final of the latter for the second consecutive year but the pair lost in three sets to <a href="/wiki/Casey_Dellacqua" title="Casey Dellacqua">Casey Dellacqua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yaroslava_Shvedova" title="Yaroslava Shvedova">Yaroslava Shvedova</a>. Despite failing to win back-to-back matches since February, Muguruza reached her second consecutive French Open quarterfinal, defeating <a href="/wiki/Angelique_Kerber" title="Angelique Kerber">Angelique Kerber</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Flavia_Pennetta" title="Flavia Pennetta">Flavia Pennetta</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> en route, before losing to the eventual runner-up, <a href="/wiki/Lucie_%C5%A0af%C3%A1%C5%99ov%C3%A1" title="Lucie Šafářová">Lucie Šafářová</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:150; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"For me if Muguruza doesn't win it this year, she's going to win this<br/>
or another Grand Slam at some point. She's not waiting, she's going<br/>
and getting it, and that's the only way you can lift a Grand Slam trophy."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/2013_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2013 Wimbledon Championships">2013 Wimbledon</a> champion <a href="/wiki/Marion_Bartoli" title="Marion Bartoli">Marion Bartoli</a>, on Muguruza after<br/>
her semi-final win over <a href="/wiki/Agnieszka_Radwa%C5%84ska" title="Agnieszka Radwańska">Agnieszka Radwańska</a> at the<br/>
<a href="/wiki/2015_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2015 Wimbledon Championships">2015 Wimbledon Championships</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Muguruza made a poor start to the <a href="/wiki/Grass_court" title="Grass court">grass court</a> season, losing in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/2015_Aegon_Classic" title="2015 Aegon Classic">Birmingham Classic</a> and the third round of the <a href="/wiki/2015_Aegon_International" title="2015 Aegon International">Eastbourne International</a> after a first round bye. However, she and Suárez Navarro won their first grass court <a href="/wiki/2015_Aegon_International_%E2%80%93_Doubles" title="2015 Aegon International – Doubles">doubles</a> title in Birmingham, defeating <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Hlav%C3%A1%C4%8Dkov%C3%A1" title="Andrea Hlaváčková">Andrea Hlaváčková</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lucie_Hradeck%C3%A1" title="Lucie Hradecká">Lucie Hradecká</a> in straight sets in the final. At the <a href="/wiki/2015_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2015 Wimbledon Championships">Wimbledon Championships</a>, Muguruza defeated 10th seed Kerber in the third round,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> 5th seed <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Wozniacki" title="Caroline Wozniacki">Caroline Wozniacki</a> in the fourth round,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> 15th seed <a href="/wiki/Timea_Bacsinszky" title="Timea Bacsinszky">Timea Bacsinszky</a> in the quarterfinals and 13th seed <a href="/wiki/Agnieszka_Radwa%C5%84ska" title="Agnieszka Radwańska">Agnieszka Radwańska</a> in the semi-finals to advance to her maiden Grand Slam final. She played against world No. 1 <a href="/wiki/Serena_Williams" title="Serena Williams">Serena Williams</a> for the title, but lost in straight sets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> After the tournament, Muguruza entered the Top 10 for the first time, moving up to world No. 9 in the <a href="/wiki/WTA_Rankings" title="WTA Rankings">WTA Rankings</a>.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2015_US_Open_Series" title="2015 US Open Series">US Open series</a>, Muguruza did not enjoy much success, dropping her opening matches in <a href="/wiki/2015_Rogers_Cup" title="2015 Rogers Cup">Toronto</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_Western_%26_Southern_Open" title="2015 Western &amp; Southern Open">Cincinnati</a> to qualifiers <a href="/wiki/Lesia_Tsurenko" title="Lesia Tsurenko">Lesia Tsurenko</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yaroslava_Shvedova" title="Yaroslava Shvedova">Yaroslava Shvedova</a> respectively. At the <a href="/wiki/2015_US_Open_(tennis)" title="2015 US Open (tennis)">US Open</a>, she recorded her first win at the tournament by defeating German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carina_Witthoeft" title="Carina Witthoeft">Carina Witthoeft</a> in the first round. However, she fell short to <a href="/wiki/Johanna_Konta" title="Johanna Konta">Johanna Konta</a> in the following round in three sets, the match was a total time of 3 hours and 23 minutes, the longest women's singles match in that tournament's history since the introduction of tiebreaker in 1970.</p>
<p>Muguruza kicked off the Asian swing at the <a href="/wiki/2015_Toray_Pan_Pacific_Open" title="2015 Toray Pan Pacific Open">Pan Pacific Open</a> where she successfully advanced to the last eight after defeating <a href="/wiki/Barbora_Str%C3%BDcov%C3%A1" title="Barbora Strýcová">Barbora Strýcová</a> before losing to eventual finalist <a href="/wiki/Belinda_Bencic" title="Belinda Bencic">Belinda Bencic</a> in straight sets. At the <a href="/wiki/2015_Wuhan_Open" title="2015 Wuhan Open">Wuhan Open</a>, Muguruza successfully cruised into her second straight quarterfinal at the event after dispatching <a href="/wiki/Sloane_Stephens" title="Sloane Stephens">Sloane Stephens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ana_Ivanovic" title="Ana Ivanovic">Ana Ivanovic</a>. She then went on to defeat the likes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anna_Karolina_Schmiedlova" title="Anna Karolina Schmiedlova">Anna Karolina Schmiedlova</a> and Kerber to reach the final where she faced <a href="/wiki/Venus_Williams" title="Venus Williams">Venus Williams</a> but was forced to retire in the second set with an ankle injury. Muguruza was able to crack the Top 5 for the first time in her career after the tournament's conclusion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2015_China_Open_(tennis)" title="2015 China Open (tennis)">China Open</a>, Muguruza breezed by <a href="/wiki/Irina_Falconi" title="Irina Falconi">Irina Falconi</a> before going the distance against <a href="/wiki/Mirjana_Lu%C4%8Di%C4%87-Baroni" title="Mirjana Lučić-Baroni">Mirjana Lučić-Baroni</a> to advance to the quarterfinals. With the win, Muguruza qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2015_WTA_Finals" title="2015 WTA Finals">WTA Finals</a> for the first time. She will be the first Spaniard to compete at the year-end championships since <a href="/wiki/Arantxa_S%C3%A1nchez_Vicario" title="Arantxa Sánchez Vicario">Arantxa Sánchez Vicario</a> in 2001. She then beat <a href="/wiki/Bethanie_Mattek-Sands" title="Bethanie Mattek-Sands">Bethanie Mattek-Sands</a> and Radwańska to advance to her maiden Premier Mandatory final. With her semifinal win over Radwańska, Muguruza cracked the Top 4 rankings where she reached a career high of world No. 4. She went on to defeat Bacsinszky in straight sets to claim her first Premier Mandatory title and her biggest title of her career.</p>
<p>Muguruza then traveled to Singapore for the <a href="/wiki/2015_WTA_Finals" title="2015 WTA Finals">WTA Finals</a>, where she went undefeated in the round robin play; beating <a href="/wiki/Petra_Kvitov%C3%A1" title="Petra Kvitová">Petra Kvitová</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angelique_Kerber" title="Angelique Kerber">Angelique Kerber</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lucie_%C5%A0af%C3%A1%C5%99ov%C3%A1" title="Lucie Šafářová">Lucie Šafářová</a>. She then lost to eventual champion <a href="/wiki/Agnieszka_Radwa%C5%84ska" title="Agnieszka Radwańska">Agnieszka Radwańska</a> in the semifinals. Muguruza also competed in doubles in Singapore, where she and her compatriot <a href="/wiki/Carla_Su%C3%A1rez_Navarro" title="Carla Suárez Navarro">Carla Suárez Navarro</a> reached the final. However, they lost to the number one seeds <a href="/wiki/Martina_Hingis" title="Martina Hingis">Martina Hingis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sania_Mirza" title="Sania Mirza">Sania Mirza</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016:_French_Open_champion.2C_world_No._2.2C_inconsistencies">2016: French Open champion, world No. 2, inconsistencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2016: French Open champion, world No. 2, inconsistencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_Roland_Garros_2016.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1032" data-file-width="763" height="271" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_Roland_Garros_2016.jpg/200px-Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_Roland_Garros_2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_Roland_Garros_2016.jpg/300px-Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_Roland_Garros_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_Roland_Garros_2016.jpg/400px-Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_Roland_Garros_2016.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza_Roland_Garros_2016.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Muguruza holds her trophy after winning the 2016 French Open</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Muguruza started her year at <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_International" title="Brisbane International">Brisbane International</a>, when she already had to retire in her first match of the tournament due to <a href="/wiki/Plantar_fasciitis" title="Plantar fasciitis">plantar fasciitis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Her next tournament was the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Open" title="Australian Open">Australian Open</a>, where she ensured a spot in the third round with straight set wins over <a href="/wiki/Anett_Kontaveit" title="Anett Kontaveit">Anett Kontaveit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Flipkens" title="Kirsten Flipkens">Kirsten Flipkens</a>, but fell to <a href="/wiki/Barbora_Str%C3%BDcov%C3%A1" title="Barbora Strýcová">Barbora Strycová</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/Fed_Cup" title="Fed Cup">Fed Cup</a>, Muguruza helped in Spain's tie against Serbia with wins over <a href="/wiki/Ivana_Jorovi%C4%87" title="Ivana Jorović">Ivana Jorovic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jelena_Jankovi%C4%87" title="Jelena Janković">Jelena Jankovic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Tennis_Championships" title="Dubai Tennis Championships">Dubai Tennis Championships</a>, Muguruza suffered another early loss as she fell to eventual semifinalist <a href="/wiki/Elina_Svitolina" title="Elina Svitolina">Elina Svitolina</a>. Her next tournament was the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Open_(tennis)" title="Qatar Open (tennis)">Qatar Open</a>, where she reached first quarterfinal of the year, defeating <a href="/wiki/Nao_Hibino" title="Nao Hibino">Nao Hibino</a> and <a href="/wiki/T%C3%ADmea_Babos" title="Tímea Babos">Timea Babos</a>, but lost then to <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Petkovic" title="Andrea Petkovic">Andrea Petkovic</a> in three sets. Next she played in <a href="/wiki/2016_BNP_Paribas_Open" title="2016 BNP Paribas Open">Indian Wells Open</a>, where she lost in her opening match against <a href="/wiki/Christina_McHale" title="Christina McHale">Christina McHale</a> after receiving first round bye. At the <a href="/wiki/2016_Miami_Open" title="2016 Miami Open">Miami Open</a>, she was close to be defeated in the opening match against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominika_Cibulkova" title="Dominika Cibulkova">Dominika Cibulkova</a> but survived in the final set. She reached the fourth round but lost to the Indian Wells Champion <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Azarenka" title="Victoria Azarenka">Victoria Azarenka</a> in two tiebreakers.</p>
<p>She kicked off the clay court season by participating the <a href="/wiki/2016_Fed_Cup_World_Group_Play-offs" title="2016 Fed Cup World Group Play-offs">Fed Cup</a> against Italy. She scored wins against <a href="/wiki/Francesca_Schiavone" title="Francesca Schiavone">Francesca Schiavone</a> and No. 7 <a href="/wiki/Roberta_Vinci" title="Roberta Vinci">Roberta Vinci</a> to help Spain enter the World Group next year. She then played in <a href="/wiki/2016_Porsche_Tennis_Grand_Prix" title="2016 Porsche Tennis Grand Prix">Stuttgart Open</a>. She reached her second quarterfinals of the season where she lost to <a href="/wiki/Petra_Kvitov%C3%A1" title="Petra Kvitová">Petra Kvitová</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/2016_Mutua_Madrid_Open" title="2016 Mutua Madrid Open">Madrid Open</a>, she lost in the second round against <a href="/wiki/Irina-Camelia_Begu" title="Irina-Camelia Begu">Irina-Camelia Begu</a>, despite serving for the match. She then went on to reach her first WTA semifinals of the season in <a href="/wiki/2016_Internazionali_BNL_d%27Italia" title="2016 Internazionali BNL d'Italia">Rome</a>, after defeating top ten opponent <a href="/wiki/Timea_Bacsinszky" title="Timea Bacsinszky">Timea Bacsinszky</a> in quarterfinals, but lost to <a href="/wiki/Madison_Keys" title="Madison Keys">Madison Keys</a> in straight sets.</p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2016_French_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Singles" title="2016 French Open – Women's Singles">French Open</a>, Muguruza unexpectedly turned her season around by going on to capture her first Grand Slam title. She lost the first set against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anna_Karolina_Schmiedlova" title="Anna Karolina Schmiedlova">Anna Karolina Schmiedlova</a> in her first round match but won in three sets. After that she easily reached her second Grand Slam final without losing a set in the next five matches, including wins over former champion <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Kuznetsova" title="Svetlana Kuznetsova">Svetlana Kuznetsova</a> in the fourth round, surprise quarterfinalist <a href="/wiki/Shelby_Rogers" title="Shelby Rogers">Shelby Rogers</a>, and former runner-up <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Stosur" title="Samantha Stosur">Sam Stosur</a> in the semifinals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In the final, she faced world No. 1 <a href="/wiki/Serena_Williams" title="Serena Williams">Serena Williams</a> in a rematch of the previous year's <a href="/wiki/2015_Wimbledon_Championships_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Singles" title="2015 Wimbledon Championships – Women's Singles">Wimbledon final</a>, and won in straight sets for her maiden major title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> She marked 14 straight sets won after losing the first she played. With the title she rose to a career high No. 2 in the WTA rankings of 6 June, 2016. She is also the first Spanish female player to win a Grand Slam title since <a href="/wiki/Arantxa_S%C3%A1nchez_Vicario" title="Arantxa Sánchez Vicario">Arantxa Sánchez Vicario</a> in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Muguruza started off the grass season by playing in her home tournament the <a href="/wiki/Mallorca_Open" title="Mallorca Open">Mallorca Open</a>, where she was the No. 1 seed. However, she suffered a first-round exit to former Wimbledon semifinalist <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Flipkens" title="Kirsten Flipkens">Kirsten Flipkens</a> in straight sets, marking the third tournament of the year where she lost in her first match played and her second consecutive loss to Flipkens on grass. Muguruza returned to grass for <a href="/wiki/2016_Wimbledon_Championships" title="2016 Wimbledon Championships">Wimbledon</a> as the second favorite with the chance to usurp the top ranking from Williams while being heralded as the leader of the next generation, following Williams' recent slump in tournament finals. Though Muguruza won her opening match against <a href="/wiki/Camila_Giorgi" title="Camila Giorgi">Camila Giorgi</a> in a high quality display, she was quickly upset by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jana_Cepelova" title="Jana Cepelova">Jana Cepelova</a> in the second round. Unable to defend her finalist points from the previous year, Muguruza regressed to world No. 3 at the end of the tournament. At the Rio Olympic Games, Muguruza arrived as one of the favorite players to win in the women's singles tennis event. She defeated <a href="/wiki/Andreea_Mitu" title="Andreea Mitu">Andreea Mitu</a> of Romania and <a href="/wiki/Nao_Hibino" title="Nao Hibino">Nao Hibino</a> of Japan to progress to the third round. However, she was defeated comprehensively by the eventual Gold medalist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%B3nica_Puig" title="Mónica Puig">Mónica Puig</a> of Puerto Rico.</p>
<p>Muguruza did not have much success during the US Open series, either. At the <a href="/wiki/2016_US_Open_(tennis)" title="2016 US Open (tennis)">US Open</a>, she suffered another second-round loss, this time to <a href="/wiki/Anastasija_Sevastova" title="Anastasija Sevastova">Anastasija Sevastova</a>. She did not fare well during the Asian Swing, with early round losses at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Toray_Pan_Pacific_Open" title="2016 Toray Pan Pacific Open">Pan Pacific Open</a> in Tokyo, the <a href="/wiki/2016_Wuhan_Open" title="2016 Wuhan Open">Wuhan Open</a> in Wuhan, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2016_China_Open" title="2016 China Open">China Open</a> in Beijing. The loss in Beijing was significant, because Muguruza was the defending champion, and she therefore dropped in ranking after the tournament. However, she still qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2016_WTA_Finals" title="2016 WTA Finals">WTA Finals</a>. Muguruza was defeated in the round robin stage, her only win coming from a three-set match against <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Kuznetsova" title="Svetlana Kuznetsova">Svetlana Kuznetsova</a>. The Spaniard ended the season ranked no. 7.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2017">2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Muguruza started the season at the <a href="/wiki/2017_Brisbane_International" title="2017 Brisbane International">Brisbane International</a>, being the no. 4 seed. She made a run to the quarterfinals after three-set wins over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sam_Stosur" title="Sam Stosur">Sam Stosur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daria_Kasatkina" title="Daria Kasatkina">Daria Kasatkina</a>, and a straight sets win over <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Kuznetsova" title="Svetlana Kuznetsova">Svetlana Kuznetsova</a>. She then retired in the first set of her semifinal match against <a href="/wiki/Aliz%C3%A9_Cornet" title="Alizé Cornet">Alizé Cornet</a> due to injury. At the <a href="/wiki/2017_Australian_Open" title="2017 Australian Open">Australian Open</a>, Muguruza beat <a href="/wiki/Marina_Erakovic" title="Marina Erakovic">Marina Erakovic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Crawford" title="Samantha Crawford">Samantha Crawford</a>, Anastasija Sevastova and <a href="/wiki/Sorana_C%C3%AErstea" title="Sorana Cîrstea">Sorana Cîrstea</a> en route to her first ever quarterfinal at the tournament. She then lost to <a href="/wiki/Coco_Vandeweghe" title="Coco Vandeweghe">Coco Vandeweghe</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_style">Playing style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Playing style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Muguruza's trademark are her flat, powerful groundstrokes off of both wings that allow her to take time away from her opponents and dictate baseline rallies. She also possesses a powerful serve that enables her to get cheap points during service games, and it is capable of reaching speeds of up to 113 mph.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Fellow tennis player <a href="/wiki/Agnieszka_Radwa%C5%84ska" title="Agnieszka Radwańska">Agnieszka Radwańska</a> describes Muguruza's playing style as being "very explosive, especially from every shot. So forehand, backhand, serve, return, everything is coming to you so fast."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Her ability to move and slide effectively on clay also leaves her noted for her clay-court prowess, having reached three consecutive quarter-finals at <a href="/wiki/French_Open" title="French Open">Roland Garros</a> from 2014 to 2016. Muguruza herself has claimed that "clay is [her] territory",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> as she feels most comfortable on the surface. However, as a result of her high-risk game style, Muguruza's inconsistency is also well discussed in the tennis community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Her game can lend itself to several unforced errors and double faults in any given match, and she often loses matches to players ranked several places below her. Under new coach Sam Sumyk, Muguruza has attempted to finish more points off at the net, which has seen mixed results.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Endorsements">Endorsements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Endorsements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Muguruza was named the ambassador for <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> Spain in June 2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> and for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBVA" title="BBVA">BBVA bank</a> in December 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Her other endorsement partners are <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babolat" title="Babolat">Babolat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rolex" title="Rolex">Rolex</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maui_Jim" title="Maui Jim">Maui Jim</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In June 2016, she was named the 14th most marketable athlete by <a href="/wiki/SportsPro" title="SportsPro">SportsPro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Doubles">Doubles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Garbi%C3%B1e_Muguruza&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Doubles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
